### Post by schmindy on 2008-09-13
Introducing La Vida, The simulation game for Linux! Recently it seems like people want a port of the sims for Linux, or a sims like game for Linux so I made the La Vida Project simply aimed at creating an open source/ free simulation game. Let me know what you think. Since I have no programing sills what so ever I can't code but I figured maybe we could make a great game! Visit [http://lavida.synthasite.com/](http://lavida.synthasite.com/) for more info. Also if you created/ know of a game like this please let me know in the comments below.

---

### Post by RIchard James13 on 2008-09-16
As a programmer I have this to say. Read this [article]("http://www.moddb.com/tutorials/24591/the-modular-release-model") for making your goals [SMART]("http://www.topachievement.com/smart.html"). 

Most games developed in the commercial world are based on a thing called a design document. This is normally a book, a few hundred pages of how everything works in the game. Of course no game starts out at a few hundred pages. You start with some simple ideas and then you flesh them out. If you are unable to program you might be able to do art. But the most important thing FOSS projects need is someone willing to lead and to persist until the job is done. In order to lead people you need a direction and that is where the design document comes in. The more detailed the document the more easier it is for programmers and artists to complete the work. 

I must warn you that having a design document will not bring programmers and artist to your project. You will need other ways to entice them in. People need a way to contribute (sourceforge or launchpad) and a way to communicate (mailing lists, IRC channels, Forums).

Now for an example of how to start fleshing the game out.
[LIST]
[*]Single or MultiPlayer?
[*]Isometric or 3D?
[*]What are you going to call your sim people? (can't be sims)
[*]What are some items of clothing they might wear?
[*]Do they have houses? How many rooms? Are they going to be multi-level?
[*]Are there doors? How do they work?
[*]What will the walls and windows look like?
[*]Can the simulated people have jobs? How can they spend their income?
[*]What is the user interface like? How does the player control their character? Can they control more than one character at a time?
[*]Will the game have a loading screen?
[*]Will you have ambient music?
[*]Will you have sound effects?
[*]What simulated emotions will the people have? How will the player be able to tell these emotions? 
[/LIST]
Remember don't answer like in the Sims. You need to write and/or draw how everything will work. As in the article above don't add too much stuff to your game at once. Start with a few small goals but be very specific as how they could be achieved. Most of the successful FOSS games started with very little but with dedication over the years have built up a significant game.

---

### Post by Vadi on 2008-09-16

### Post by smd0665 on 2009-02-18
Hi. Great idea. I was hoping to start something like this too but, I'm not a programmer either, unfortunately. Like RIchard James13 said, a lot of thought goes into it before programming. I have been thinking about what the game would be like - feel free to use any of my ideas. 

First of all, I was thinking it would be good to start with a text only version, including random events and characters. Once everything worked, then I would consider graphics. There would be a list of attributes. Such as:

Age
1.	Baby
2.	Infant
3.	Teen
4.	Adult
5.	Mature

Body
1.	Skinny
2.	Lean
3.	Plump

Hair color
1.	Light brown
2.	Dark brown
3.	Light blond
4.	Dark blond
5.	Red
6.	Purple
7.	Grey

Hair Length
1.	Bald
2.	Short
3.	Long
4.	Extra Long

House Color
1.	White
2.	Beige
3.	Yellow
4.	Brick
5.	Blue
6.	Grey

House Size &#8211; flexible, based on spending

All Merchandise (brand)
1.	Krappi® &#8211; slogan:&#8220;We Get the Job Done&#8221;
2.	A.D. Equate® &#8211; slogan:&#8220;We&#8217;re Better&#8221;
3.	Elite® &#8211; slogan:&#8220;When Money is Not an Issue&#8221;

Happiness
1.	Fun 
a)	Activities
b)	Music
c)	Television
d)	Computing

2.	Comfort
a)	Couch
b)	Bed
c)	Chair

3.	Relationships
a)	Friendship
b)	Friendship with "benefits"
c)	Love

4. Career
a)	Medical
b)	Clerical
c)	Education 
d)	Construction
e)	Religious

The character you are playing would start with a house and some money. He/she can get a job and use money for items/upgrades.

### Post by CharmyBee on 2009-08-08
> **Mickeysofine1972 said:**
> MD2 model format would be best as thats the quickest i can implement

MD2 is ugly and very limited also MD3.  You will have a dead or difficult project if you only support MD2 or MD3.

I'd recommend MD5 instead, since then you can have externalized animations shared by many humanoid models. Sauerbraten does MD5. This is the best format I can think of for this kind of game.

---

### Post by xakh on 2009-08-09
The armor is pretty integrated with the body, I figured since we would need to have a tolerance for some wacky stuff on characters anyway, we could just start with the guy in the space suit, than do a different one later. I'll work on giving it a full UV map, and put things like caution tape and stuff on the body of the character, to make sure that it's very clear he's the testing model only, and that screenshots with him in it will obviously not be in the end production. Oh, I also have an old model of a desk, a few old chairs, and some couch models I can contribute, as soon as someone links me to a good site to host my stuff on.

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2009-08-13
Hi all

Just relised I had a bug!

Python OpenGL in ubuntu doesnt have glVertexf !

I fixed it though so if you want to give it a go you need the following python packages:

python-opengl
pygame

once you install those you need to go to the la-vida folder and type :

python la-vida.py

after a few seconds you will see a sim landscape, use w,s and the arrow keys to have a look arround, (although a bit limited atm)

Mike

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2009-11-17
Hi All

I just updated the code with the ability to click anywhere in the game world and get the exact coordinates you clicked in 3dc space.

So now things are getting bigger I thought I would create a sourceforge page complete with subversion repository here:

[http://sourceforge.net/projects/la-vida/](http://sourceforge.net/projects/la-vida/)

You can get the latest code and resources by installing subversion through the package manager and I recommend rapidsvn from there too as its the best subversion client I've used.

to download manually open a terminal and type:

```
svn co https://la-vida.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/la-vida la-vida
```
then to run:
```

cd la-vida/trunk
python la-vida.py

```I use wingIDE for python development as its pretty nifty and also the one I work with all the time in my job.

I've included the project file for wing so you may find it easier to get yourself the free version of wing 101 from their website.

Mike

---

### Post by gsmanners on 2009-12-28
The cool thing about The Sims is how you juggle a sim's Motives along with what you're planning for them to accomplish. Motives are a group of tangible and intangible "needs" that tell you roughly how the sim feels:

Hunger, Comfort, Bladder, Hygiene, Energy <-- tangible
Fun, Social, Environment <-- intangible

You can add other motives, of course, the point is that you have mundane tasks that need to be carried out. For autonomy, it's probably a good idea to just default to making "Fun" the major motive unless some other motive is starting to become an issue. This keeps the sim interesting to the player (it's more fun to watch someone endlessly dancing than to watch someone just lying around all the time).

With Sims 2, they added Wants and Fears, which were just general descriptions of things that could happen which would contribute to that sim's "aspiration" (their ego meter). They really tried to focus on the Wants/Fears and tried to hide the motives by default, but that didn't really work out like they thought. The main thing that made it fun was handling the motives.

I guess my point here is to decide how Dudes or whatever are motivated, and that will make the game fun.

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2009-12-28
Yep I couldn't agree more.

### Post by gsmanners on 2009-12-29
For disorders, Sims 2 did some "immaturity" (red ego meter) and "desperation" (red motive meter). It wasn't too convincing, but in Pets they implemented "Learned Behavior" tokens which also included a variety of bad behaviors (which sadly only applied to animal sims).

I like the idea of "Learned Behaviors" myself. A system whereby the player can provide feedback regarding whether a behavior is considered good or bad might be fun, too.

---

### Post by matchett808 on 2009-12-29
Yeah, learnedd behaviour sounds good to me too....lol

...one though was on the "needs" subject - the most important needs should obviously be things like hunger etc.....

...just as an oddball you could through in some medical issues too! like the ability to break a leg (when doing something "stupid") and of course die....and if you die you should stay there untill the authorities are informed and (if your game has the ability to order 1 dude to kill another) chance of being caught and punnished lol

---

### Post by gsmanners on 2009-12-30
Dead sims were actually a source of technical problems for Sims 2. Dead sim IDs would clog the neighbor list and cause "too many iteration" errors. They ended up bumping the number of iterations an object could use without idling up to 100,000 because of that. :P

If you have a system like Memories, it would be a good idea for Dudes to have unique DudeIDs, but I don't think keeping them around in a list of Dudes in the world (or whatever) is a good idea. Maybe you could have dead Dudes move on to another World, and keep separate ID lists or something like that.

---

### Post by matchett808 on 2009-12-31
would the easy way not be to have a database with uid and status (dead or alive lol with dead also having a 'link or something' to an entry that details where the dude is etc....) 

Once a dude died it would be removed from the database by "the authorities" after they have collected the body.......

---

### Post by dagoth_pie on 2009-12-31
what if you wanted to have their ghosts come back to haunt the place they died, then you'd need to keep them in the database after death, wouldn't you?

---

### Post by gsmanners on 2010-01-01
Not necessarily. Say you have two sets of data, Alive and Dead. For the recently departed, you could create another object that would provide a link between the two. That object would summon the ghost and also retrieve the ghost back into their world.

In Sims 1 and 2, they used tombstones to trigger hauntings, but you could really use anything, and not just as a trigger. If you have two (or more) sets of data, you could even use living Dudes as portals between worlds if you really wanted.

Unlinking and deleting a Dude reference would be akin to eternal damnation, and I don't think you really want a game to go *there*. :P

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-03-02

---

### Post by gsmanners on 2010-03-02
About the menus, pie menus are pretty standard for all The Sims games, but they always seemed like an idea that was impractical. In the various EPs for Sims 2, they added the ability to have any number of sub menus, and that just added to the amount of clicking you do with the mouse (which made the game less usable). I would therefore suggest a nice normal rectangular menu. :)

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-03-02
> **gsmanners said:**
> About the menus, pie menus are pretty standard for all The Sims games, but they always seemed like an idea that was impractical. In the various EPs for Sims 2, they added the ability to have any number of sub menus, and that just added to the amount of clicking you do with the mouse (which made the game less usable). I would therefore suggest a nice normal rectangular menu. :)

Ok thats a good point, but is it possible to make a nice way of selecting objects and actions ?

I dont really think we should have pie menus anyhow as thats just copying. How about a different shaped menu that makes that sort of thing easier?

Mike

---

### Post by gsmanners on 2010-03-02
It all depends on how you design the game. The design for The Sims was genius. You highlight objects and change the mouse cursor on mouseover events, then bring up an icon of what you have selected when you click on it, then surround the icon with menu options. All of that simply bespeaks the underlying design having objects that interact with other objects. You select the "me" object with the plumbbob and select the "target" with your mouse. Then the menu item you select is the interaction.

All of this is just to say simply this: a menu should be designed to fit its purpose. I'm not saying this is how you make the game work. You can make it work however you feel like and then it would make sense to design a UI that fits that design.

---

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-03
Ok. First we should specify a goal for the game.

Why does the player what he does?

Reach a life goal?

For example:


[LIST]
[*]Family  happiness
[*]Professional  success
[/LIST]

Some ideas?

[LIST]

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-03-03
Well I think there are a few goals really:

1) Move into a new house with your new dude and get used to the experience
2) Get used to interacting with other dudes/activities
3) Build up your home
4) Start building a lifestyle and hopefully succeed in it

So the interface has to be something that can work for all of those tasks, which is why the pie menus work for the sims. They make interaction quick and easy and let you focus on the task rather than learning loads of different ways to 'configure' things. Theres a definite lack of the feeling of 'configuring' and more a feeling of 'doing'.

Mike

---

### Post by Nevon on 2010-03-03
> **Noraphalem said:**
> [LIST]
[*]Food
[*]Water (Should we seperate this?)
[*]Recovery, Relaxing, Sleep
[*]Comfort
[/LIST]
Any futher ideas?
No need to over complicate things. Just look as Maslow's hierarchy of needs.

[img]http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Maslow%27s_Hierarchy_of_Needs.svg/450px-Maslow%27s_Hierarchy_of_Needs.svg.png[/img]

From that, we can get (in order of importance):
[LIST]
[*]Food/water (sustenance)
[*]Sleep
[*]Execretion
[*]Hygien (basically "health" in the hierarchy of needs)
[*]"Social" (a combination of sex, intimacy, security of the family, etc.)
[*]Creativity (this could also be "fun")
[/LIST]

And then come the self-actualization stuff - like goals, achievements etc.

### Post by Nevon on 2010-03-03
> **Mickeysofine1972 said:**
> Yep thats more or less what i was thinking without actually having the thoery lol

Mike

One thing that hit me as something that is not present in the hierarchy of needs, but that I think plays a major role in modern society, is stress. Or well, I suppose it is in there in a way (what with employment, resources, morality, respect from others, etc.). In The Sims I think they've implemented stress as the overall mood bar. If the sim is hungry and dirty, the mood bar will be lowered. But other things that don't directly affect the needs can also affect the mood. For example if you do really poorly at work, your mood is lowered. If a family member dies, your mood is lowered. And so on.

Maybe that could wait for later, but its definitely something to keep in mind. I understand the want to branch off from The Sims, but human needs are always the same, so there's no sense in being different *just because*.

---

### Post by gsmanners on 2010-03-03
Stress in Sims 2 was a byproduct of aspiration (which could go from red at the bottom to green, gold and platinum as you go up). If a Sim's aspiration was in the red, they would tend to behave with "immaturity" or even totally freak out and need imaginary psychotherapy. If their aspiration was in platinum, their mood meter would go full platinum as well (which would wreak havoc on the whole system of free will they used).

---

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-04
> **ndefontenay said:**
> Hi.

Is there a homepage or a launchpad.net page for la vida where we can get the latest news and download?

I would love to test it and probably develop a little bit too.

Nico

At the moment there is a SVN repository on sourceforge.net.

You can check it out:

svn co [https://la-vida.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/la-vida](https://la-vida.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/la-vida) la-vida

But you need the package subversion!

To run the game type the following in a terminal:

cd </home/<user>/la-vida/trunk>
python2.5 ./la-vida.py

or

cd </home/<user>/la-vida/trunk>
python2.6 ./la-vida.py

### Post by Bölvaður on 2010-03-08
For gameplay I suggest handing out cards with objectives. There are some board games that have a system like that, RISK for an example. You are given (lets say 3) cards with some tasks with a random number of social points you gain for completing the task. Those kind of tasks might be "Befriend Harry Snitschell" and "Get a goldfish".
Then there would be 1 or 2 other cards with big tasks such as. "Have a baby with a celebrity" and "Rob a bank", "Marry Yoda".

The points you get for completing such tasks might be called social points, which you could use to buy some sort of social manipulation, like being closer friends with someone... like Yoda, make Yoda's wife angry at him or get sent money from one's grandmother

with this you can have either an sp or an mmo where the world is your ally/opponent

---

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-09
Ok some thoughs regarding gameplay:

Life mode:[INDENT]First person view and alternativ third person view
Look ... Mouse movement
Walk/Run ... WASD
Use ... Left mouse button
Leaf action menu ... Right mouse button
Switch between possible actions ... Mouse wheel
[/INDENT]Build mode:[INDENT]Isometric view
Move camera ... Right mouse button and mouse movement
Rotate camera ... Right mouse button, shift or alt button and mouse movement
Zoom ... Mouse wheel
Action ... Left mouse button
[/INDENT]Any thoughs?

[/URL]

### Post by Nevon on 2010-03-09
> **Mickeysofine1972 said:**
> Well I like most of it but I dunno about WASD for controls or having a first-person angle :-S

Its all about looking ove the big picture and being in control from that perspective I think

Mike

I know I'm not really involved in this project at all, but I couldn't agree more. There's no real added value in having a third person view and direct control over your dudes using wasd. You're not supposed to show your dudes exactly **how** to do things - just what they should accomplish. For example, you say: "Make pancakes". You don't say: "Go to the refrigerator, get the milk and some eggs. Then go to the pantry on your right and get some flour, baking powder, salt, and sugar. Then mix it all together in a bowl that you get from the cupboard on your left, etc."

Also, from experience I can say that you do not want to switch actions using the mouse wheel. It feels very unnatural, especially if you're using a trackpad rather than a mouse.

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-03-09
Noted :D

Mike

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-10
Ok I have added wall, wall with window and door models. With uv maps but currently no textures. The game should assign the right textures (with the different surfaces for example wallpapers) on the wall model.

There are three materials on the wall model.

1. wall ... the wall itself. only shown on the upside and downside. Texture is fix. For example bricks.

2. wall_inside ... the first side with the changing surface.

3. wall_outside ... the second

So we can assign two different textures on a single wall section.

And the wall with window model hasthe same materials as the wall model except the material window_border.

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-03-17
> **Noraphalem said:**
> Great idea! ;)

:?: Question :?:
Is it possible to load dynamicly textures into one model.

Like:

[LIST=1]
[*]Create a wall object
[*]Load the wall model "wall.obj"
[*]Link texture "wall_0.png" for the inside
[*]Link texture "wall_1.png" for the outside
[*]Create a new wall object
[*]Load the wall model "wall.obj"
[*]Link texture "wall_2.png" for the inside
[*]Link texture "wall_3.png" for the outside
[/LIST]
[[IMG]http://img228.imageshack.us/img228/4046/wall2y.png[/IMG]]("http://img228.imageshack.us/i/wall2y.png/")

Well I've been thinking about this one myself...

I reckon you could load the wall textures and then draw them on to one side or other of a square texture then map that onto the object:

--------------------                 ----------------------------------------
|                       |                 |                                                |
|  wall texture    |                 |                                                |
|          in          |                 |                opengl                      |
|     memory      |                 |                 texture                     |
|                       |                 |                                                |
|                       |                 |                                                |
|                       |        ->     |                                                |
|                       |                 |                                                |
|                       |                 |                                                |
|                       |                 |                                                |
|                       |                 |                                                |
|                       |                 |                                                |
|                       |                 |                                                |
--------------------                 ----------------------------------------

then we can have one side mapped to one half of the square and another on the other side :D

Its all theory though atm as this is something I'm working on atm

Mike

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-03-19
> **_h_ said:**
> Is this game going to include various graphic level profiles such as custom, lowest, low, normal, high, extra high and the sorts?

Could include GFX presets into the config file too.

Well I reckon the game will recognise different settings as a standard, fast or custom combinations to yeah that should be in there but also the options themselves shou be there in the [GRAPHICS] section:

lavida.conf
```

[GRAPHICS]
mode=1024x768
fullscreen=YES
shadows=NO
shaders=NO
level=FAST

[SOUND]
music=OFF   # also could be set to 1 to 100?

```

just like a standard .cfg file really for quake etc.

Mike

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-19
Ok some code:

```
class Configuration:
    def __init__():
        ' To do

    def LoadConfigurationFile():
        ConfigurationFile = Open("./la-vida.config", "r")

        while( CurrentLineContent != None ):
            CurrentLineContent = ConfigurationFile.ReadLine()
            if( CurrentLineContent.Upper == "[GRAPHICS]" ):
                CurrentSection = "GRAPHICS"
            elif( CurrentLineContent.Upper == "[SOUND]" ):
                CurrentSection == "SOUND"
            else:
                if( CurrentLineContent.Count("ResWidth=") >= 1 ):
                    ResWidth = CurrentLineContent.Strip( "ResWidth=" )
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("ResHeight=") >= 1 ):
                    ResHeight = CurrentLineContent.Strip( "ResHeight=" )
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Fullscreen=") >= 1 ):
                    if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Fullscreen=" ) == "On" ):
                        ' Set fullscreen on
                    if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Fullscreen=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set fullscreen off
                    else:
                        ' Set fullscreen off
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Effects=") >= 1 ):
                    if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Effects=" ) == "On" ):
                        ' Set sound effects on
                    if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Effects=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set sound effects off
                    else:
                        ' Set sound effects on
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Music=") >= 1 ):
                    if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Music=" ) == "On" ):
                        ' Set music on
                    if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Music=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set music off
                    else:
                        ' Set music on

        ConfigurationFile.Close()

    def SaveConfigurationFile():
        ' To do
```It is not finished yet. More is coming tomorrow.

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-21
1. Last test of svn checkout was fine! :biggrin:

2. I have uploaded an oven model plus textures and uv maps.

3. I have corrected "data/enviroment" --> "data/environment" plus py files (I hope I have nothing forgotten ;-))

 4. And last, some reviewed code for the configuration class:

```
class Configuration:
    def __init__():
        ' To do

    def LoadConfigurationFile():
        ConfigurationFile = Open("./la-vida.config", "r")

        while( CurrentLineContent != None ):
            CurrentLineContent = ConfigurationFile.ReadLine()
            if( CurrentLineContent.Upper == "[GRAPHICS]" ):
                CurrentSection = "GRAPHICS"
            elif( CurrentLineContent.Upper == "[SOUND]" ):
                CurrentSection = "SOUND"
            else:
                if( CurrentLineContent.Count("ResWidth=") >= 1 ):
                    NewResWidth = CurrentLineContent.Strip( "ResWidth=" )
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("ResHeight=") >= 1 ):
                    NewResHeight = CurrentLineContent.Strip( "ResHeight=" )
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Fullscreen=") >= 1 ):
                    if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Fullscreen=" ) == "On" ):
                        ' Set fullscreen on
                    elif( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Fullscreen=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set fullscreen off
                    else:
                        ' Set fullscreen off
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Effects=") >= 1 ):
                    NewEffectsVolume = CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Effects=" )
                    ' if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Effects=" ) == "On" ):
                        ' Set sound effects on
                    ' elif( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Effects=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set sound effects off
                    ' else:
                        ' Set sound effects on
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Music=") >= 1 ):
                    NewMusicVolume = CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Music=" )
                    ' if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Music=" ) == "On" ):
                        ' Set music on
                    ' elif( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Music=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set music off
                    ' else:
                        ' Set music on

        ConfigurationFile.Close()

    def SaveConfigurationFile( NewResWidth, NewResHeight, NewMode, NewEffectsVolume, NewMusicVolume ):
        ConfigurationFile = Open("./la-vida.config", "w")

        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "[GRAPHICS]" )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "ResWidth=%s" % ( NewResWidth ) )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "ResHeight=%s" % ( NewResHeight ) )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "Fullscreen=%s" % ( NewMode ) )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "[SOUND]" )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "Effects=%s" % ( NewEffectsVolume ) )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "Music=%s" % ( NewMusicVolume ) )

        ConfigurationFile.Close()
```

                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Fullscreen=") >= 1 ):
                    if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Fullscreen=" ) == "On" ):
                        ' Set fullscreen on
                    elif( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Fullscreen=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set fullscreen off
                    else:
                        ' Set fullscreen off
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Effects=") >= 1 ):
                    NewEffectsVolume = CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Effects=" )
                    ' if( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Effects=" ) == "On" ):
                        ' Set sound effects on
                    ' elif( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Effects=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set sound effects off
                    ' else:
                        ' Set sound effects on
                elif( CurrentLineContent.Count("Music=") >= 1 ):
                    NewMusicVolume = CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Music=" )

                        ' Set music on
                    ' elif( CurrentLineContent.Strip( "Music=" ) == "Off" ):
                        ' Set music off

                        ' Set music on

    def SaveConfigurationFile( NewResWidth, NewResHeight, NewMode, NewEffectsVolume, NewMusicVolume ):

        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "Fullscreen=%s" % ( NewMode ) )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "[SOUND]" )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "Effects=%s" % ( NewEffectsVolume ) )
        ConfigurationFile.WriteLine( "Music=%s" % ( NewMusicVolume ) )

        ConfigurationFile.Close()
```

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-03-23
Well I aim to have house building and furniture placement done within the next 2 to 3 months.

Thats the most complex part unfortunately as making realtime editable house configurations is a bit messy on the combining object side. Its really expensive on the video card if you cant combine them.

I'm starting to get some workable stuff going so its improving in terms of keeping a constant 30fps on my system, ( a toshiba laptop and a gf6 series system ), Ideally you wont need a super beast machine to play.

After that the behaviours code is less trivial and a lot easier to get your head round; in fact if anyone would like to have a stab at a class that manages that sort of stuff we can start that now and later refine it.

As for things like getting the dudes to cook and walk up stairs, we need content contributors to provide animations and sound effects etc so all contributions are welcome

I think thats enough to cover what might hopefully get this done by about september, ( thats a hopeful guess )

its up to the community to contribute and I urge everyone who wants this to happen to see if they have even a small amount to help with.

Mike

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-25
> **Nevon said:**
> 
At this point I don't quite see the use for the steps. As I said before, you don't want to tell your sim to go to the cupboard, get flour, salt, milk, sugar, butter and eggs, mix them together in a bowl, etc. You just want to tell it to make pancakes.
I agree in that.

Concerning "action" menu I would say a menu in 3D space over the object is the best best way to do it.

Concerning "mood/stresslevel":

Mood: Changes every day and last the whole day. It influences all activities.
(From 0 To 75)

Feeling type: Defines the different emotions like happyness, anger, ...

Feeling intensity: Defines the intensity of that feeling.
(From 0 To 25)

For example:

Mood: 73
Feeling: Anger
Intensity: 13

Means the avatar is basicly in good mood but something annoys him/her.

```


if( Feeling == "Happyness" ):
      if( Mood + FeelingIntensity >= 75 ):
            Result = "Success"
      else:
            Result = "Failure"

elif( Feeling == "Sadness" ):
      if( Mood - FeelingIntensity >= 50 ):
            Result = "Success"
      else:
            Result = "Failure"

elif( Feeling == "Anger" ):
      if( Mood - FeelingIntensity >= 75 ):
            Result = "Success"
      else:
            Result = "Failure"
...

```[COLOR=DarkRed][COLOR=Black]

Your thoughs?
[/COLOR] [/COLOR]

---

### Post by OgreProgrammer on 2010-03-25
While the GUI is early in development, can I make a usability request?

Lately I have been interested in doing a web comic, and I was looking at applications to do scenes and screen shots as a way to ease authoring. I then recalled that people used the sims 1 to tell stories. Then I remembered this project. Apparently its still moving along... good!

Anyway. To the point. The ability to turn off all gui displays will open up interest to a wider variety of users. These sorts of applications are not games per se, but a singular sort of story telling, and sometimes a stage to tell stories to others.

I confess: I dont know IF I would use it, but it shouldnt take much to set up a toggle. Many sorts of games have such a feature for screen shots.

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-03-25
> **OgreProgrammer said:**
> While the GUI is early in development, can I make a usability request?

Lately I have been interested in doing a web comic, and I was looking at applications to do scenes and screen shots as a way to ease authoring. I then recalled that people used the sims 1 to tell stories. Then I remembered this project. Apparently its still moving along... good!

Anyway. To the point. The ability to turn off all gui displays will open up interest to a wider variety of users. These sorts of applications are not games per se, but a singular sort of story telling, and sometimes a stage to tell stories to others.

I confess: I dont know IF I would use it, but it shouldnt take much to set up a toggle. Many sorts of games have such a feature for screen shots.

Indeed

How about if we made a screenshot button that only takes a shot of the scene and doesnt include the gui?

Mike

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-26
I think we should use a low, medium and high resolution version of the textures/game data:

Low: 128x128 px
Medium: 256x256 px
High: 512x512 px

Seperate the game source code/program form the data:

la-vida.tar.gz --> ./la-vida/..
la-vida-data-low.tar.gz --> ./la-vida/data
la-vida-data-medium.tar.gz --> ./la-vida/data
la-vida-data-high.tar.gz --> ./la-vida/data

Each player can choose wich package he/she wants/needs in relation to the hardware specification.

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-03-26
Whats about a contribution guide line?

File format guide line:

2D Graphics (GUI images, textures, ...)

[LIST]
[*] Portable Network Graphics (PNG) for raster graphics
[*] Scaleable Vector Graphics (SVG) for vector graphics
[/LIST]
    Please NO

[LIST]
[*] Microsoft Windows/OS/2 Bitmap (BMP),
[*] ... (Convert it please.)
[/LIST]
 
3D Graphics (Models, uv maps, material, animation, ...)

[LIST]
[*] Wavefront Object/Material (OBJ/MTL) for 3D models, uv maps, materials and animation
[*] Support MD2 any longer?
[/LIST]
    Please NO

[LIST]
[*]3D Studio Max (MAX/3DS),
[*] ... (Convert it please.)
[/LIST]
 
Sounds (Effects, music, ...)

[LIST]
[*] OGG Vorbis (OGG)
[/LIST]
    Please NO

[LIST]
[*] Microsoft RIFF Wave (WAV),
[*] Microsoft Windows Media Audio (WMA),
[*] MPEG-1 Audio Layer 3 (MP3),
[*] ... (Convert it please.)
[/LIST]
  Your thoughs?

---

### Post by myromance123 on 2010-04-06
I'm not an art student so I actually don't know what a Visual Style Guide is or looks like :P

 At most I can offer the basic settings I use in GIMP when making the icons, which are as follows:
> Paintbrush - Opacity between 40-50.
Scale - 0.01 to 0.10 for fine detail.
Brush - standard Circle (11)

Mode - Normal

Blend tool
Opacity between 40-50 for general coloring
		100 for light reflection
Gradient - FG to BG (RGB)

Image size - 128x128
Background - transparent.
Format - .PNG Yep, pretty darn basic settings.

What I'm trying to go for in the icons I guess is somewhere between realistic and yet not picture perfect. The proportions of the objects are as close as possible to real world objects (at least I try to make them like that) with colors that define the objects appearance not being too far from reality. Not going for a cartoonish or toon-like look. Don't know how to go for that look.


Maybe Nevon or Noraphalem can assist in giving guidelines?
They seem to have a better background in arts (or at least it looks like that :) ).

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-04-13
Ok thats starting to look awesome :D

When I say no tables I mean your page layout should be like this:

```

<html>
<head>
</head>
<body>
   <div id="wholepage">
      <div id="header">blah blah blah</div>
      <div id="content">
         <div id="left_column">blah blah blah</div>
         <div id="right_column">blah blah blah</div>
      </div>
      <div id="footer">blah blah blah</div>
   </div>
</body>
</html>

```

anything in the left or right columns should be wrapped in a H tag or a P for spacing

that way we can apply css formating and it will not need any editing if we change the designs font or spacings etc

I really like how its developing though

Mike

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-04-14
After some research how to do a mesh for the avatar I have to report the following:

I want really reuse the mesh out of MakeHuman because it has a very high quality level. So I have experimented a bit:

I am able to export the mesh from MakeHuman and import the socalled Proxy mesh which contains only 1500 vertices which is not much for an homaniod mesh. And it is still rigged!!! :biggrin: But it is a bit buggy and don't have any uv map. So it is a pain to use that thing! #-o

A short summary:

Vertices: appr. 1500

Benefits:

[LIST]
[*]Complete mesh
[*]Rigged
[/LIST]

Disadvantages:

[LIST]
[*]Bugs
[*]No UV map
[/LIST]

Should I use it? What are your thoughs?

---

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-04-16
First a little overview of the "Avatar" class:

```
CLASS "Avatar"
 -----PROPERTIES-----
 PROPERTY "FirstName"
 PROPERTY "LastName"
 PROPERTY "BirthDate"
 PROPERTY "BirthSign"
 PROPERTY "Age"
 PPOPERTY "Mood"
 PROPERTY "EmotionType"
 PROPERTY "EmotionIntensity"
 PROPERTY "Activities" (List, Arrey, ???)
 PROPERTY "Model"
 PROPERTY "PositionX"
 PROPERTY "PositionY"
 PROPERTY "PositionZ"
 -----METHODES-----
 METHODE "GetFirstName"
 METHODE "SetFirstName"
 METHODE "GetLastName"
 METHODE "SetLastName"
 METHODE "GetBirthDate"
 METHODE "SetBirthDate"
 METHODE "GetBirthSign"
 METHODE "SetBirthSign"
 METHODE "GetAge"
 METHODE "SetAge"
 METHODE "GetMood"
 METHODE "SetMood"
 METHODE "GetEmotionType"
 METHODE "SetEmotionType"
 METHODE "GetEmotionIntensity"
 METHODE "SetEmotionIntensity"
 METHODE "DoActivity" (From List, Arrey, ???)
 METHODE "AddActivity" (To)
 METHODE "GetModel"
 METHODE "SetModel"
 METHODE "GetPosition"
 METHODE "SetPosition"
```This has surely to get extanded.

Concerning avatar model:

We have two ways to handle the avatar model creating:

1) Ship some premade ones and give the player the possibility to create and use his/her own.

2) Ship an in-game avatar editor. This is very much work.

My idea is to interact/interoperate with MakeHuman. They plan to implement a low poly exporter (OBJ and MHX(MakeHuman eXchange format)) so we can use this in future. MHX is designed to exchange the data with Blender. Maybe we can use this interface.

---

I plan to make a skinning texture that will allow clothes to be made so we can create shirts and stuff so they will be added using that method.

Mike

That way you dont have to settle for the average shaped avatar you can skinny ones and short/tall ones etc.

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-04-18
If your happy to do that then thats great; I'll see how it goes and if I think it took complex we can perhaps review the code and look for the parts we do like.

Mike

EDIT: I've just finished making the manifest loading system which will allow content to be added without having to code.

All you do is add the following to the data/evironment/manifests/default.man file:

```
OBJECT:<path>:<position>:<scale>
```

path is the location within the data folder e.g. environment/manmade/cheese/cheese.obj

position is a 3d vector position like 1.0,10.0,3.0 with no spaces between the commas

and scale is a floating point value like 0.4 ( 0.4 seems to be about right for most models actually :D )

---

### Post by uylug on 2010-04-18
Seems to be a great idea to me. I just hope that you get the chance to meet a few developers before starting because programming a project like this could take forever and you'll end up not finishing it if you do it on your own.

So I suggest you to design a few things, write them down in a paper, make some drawings, take some programming tutorials (c++) and then start coding. Create a subversion code repository to avoid surprises and make a bugzilla server and have other people test your stuff.

### Post by JDShu on 2010-04-23
Hey! I felt like practicing some coding and checked out your project. As an exercise, I edited the program so that the the wsad keys makes the camera move forward depending on the camera angle instead of simply incrementing the x or z coordinates. Its just some simple trig that I'm sure you guys could have done too, but would you like me to send a patch? I've never participated in an open source project so forgive me if I sound noob.

Edit:
Actually, I just put it in my dropbox. Tell me if I'm doing something wrong or unnecessary, no need to be gentle :D

[http://dl.dropbox.com/u/5597392/lavida_camera_mod.diff](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/5597392/lavida_camera_mod.diff)

---

### Post by myromance123 on 2010-04-24
Wow thats a really cool contribution JDShu :D

 I also just learned how to handle .diff files using patch. It works like a charm. I was always wondering if the wsad keys could move according to the camera angle instead.
 
 Thats really cool man :D
I can't judge the code however, I'm a beginner at python. I'll leave it to Mike ;)

 Thanks for the awesome contribution JDShu!
Keep it coming if you can :)

PS: for those who want to test it out but don't know how, do this:
  1. Put the lavida_camera_mod.diff into the GameApp folder of la-vida
  2. Open up a terminal and cd to the GameApp folder.
  3. Run this,
  ```
patch < lavida_camera_mod.diff
```
  4. Then run la-vida like normal, using 'python la_vida.py'.

If, for whatever reason, you want to remove the patch simply go back to GameApp folder through the terminal. This time run this:
```
patch -R < lavida_camera_mod.diff
```

Hmmm I think we need to mature a little before we can support this sort of stuff to be honest.

We have quite a few things that a far more important in terms of features, ( I'm not saying not a great idea though ), so it may be a long time before we get there on that one.

I'm really trying to keep it Python only but I'm starting to see the need for some C/C++ to make that sort of things fast enough.

Not that anyone will see that difference if they are just a Python programmer trying to mess about with the code.

You dont have to contribute either but you could learn something and I'd be really pleased to hear anyones experiences even if they have nothing to give back.

### Post by JDShu on 2010-04-25
Alright, it looks like I'm going to need to familiarize myself properly with OpenGL. Tell me if this is already dealt with, but it looks to me like the currently there is no proper translation from 2D coordinates to world coordinates, so I can't just pass in the mouse position into the Draw() method for TexturedRect. Hence, maybe I should look into changing Draw() so that it can do this? If yes, I've got some learning to do :P

EDIT:

Alright, playing around some more, it seems to me that running BeginDrawing2d() and then invoking TexturedRect.Draw() seems to draw onto a "canvas" that is larger than the what the camera sees. Is there some way to shrink the 2d canvas to the camera size?

### Post by DrWer2 on 2010-04-25
Hi, sorry for budding in like this. I have been following this topic for a while now, saying nothing due to lack of anything to say. Any ways, I have just thought of an idea that I have decided to throw out there. It has to do with skills.

I assume that like the Sims, Dudes will have skills that help to make them who they are. My idea is that there should be a skill boness that is added to the base value of a dudes skills. This boness comes from a percentage of the base skills of another dude that this dude has as a good friend or family member.

This explanation may be confusing so here is a real world example.

My father was an airplane mechanic and an all around handyman. When I was old enough to hold a wrench I was in the garage helping my dad fix old lawnmowers cars and other things. If we weren't fixing broken things we "modified" them to work better. Most of the time the modifications worked and if they didn't it meant more father son time. Normal conversation at home and with friends of my father where centered around airplanes, cars, and ideas about how to make them work better. For these reasons I know more about these topics than most people. I am not saying that I know as much as my father just by being around him, but it has influenced my life.

This being said, me and my dad are vastly different people. I am fairly good with computers, computers literally freeze up when my dad comes near them. My father got C's in school and I was a strait A student. My dad likes Nascar and football. I use that time for a nap. 

What do you think? :)

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-05-05
Ok heres an update:

Thanks to JD we are now sporting some nice new menu functionality also looking forward to having the dudes walk around fully configurable houses that you can pretty much make any design you like with.

We are looking to add all this in the main trunk of the game over the next few weeks to keep your eyes peeled.

After that we plan to make use of the new event handling system that should make it possible for dudes and dudettes to respond to each others choices and actions. Making party activities possible, ( like taking a swim in the pool or having a dance with Mrs Dudette from down the street :D )

We're feeling pretty good about hitting the September version 1.0 goal and think we might even get there sooner. Maybe we will put more features in with the extra time!

Mike

---

### Post by JDShu on 2010-05-05
> **DrWer2 said:**
> Is it in the plan to make different wall types(brick, wood, stone,etc.) cost more or take longer to build?

Another thing with prices. Are we going for realism or will the prices be kept lower than normal for simplicity?

Under the assumption that there are different wall types (and I think there will be, but Mike will have a more concrete answer), I think there would be varying prices, yes.

For the second question, I would vote that the price of walls be low in comparison to other things you buy. It would be irritating to try to earn lots of money to buy one chunk of wall. On the other hand, if we wanted to be REALLY realistic, then maybe we can make the dudes and dudettes take out mortgages or rent their living space :D

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-05-06
Initially, we will ba making different wall type which can be applied on one side of the walls, however, there will not be the ability to have each individual wall segment have different wall coverings.

Later on after that release I plan to make it more configurable but I want get it to a basic functioning system first.

As for costs? well bricks and plain walls will be the lowest costing but will be charged initially at a rate of the type times the whole number of wall segments for that floor. Later this will be individual segments as the rendering matures to per segment texturing.

Mike

---

Mike

The stuff that (might be) in C/C++ is the 3D animation code - the intensive graphical stuff. Mike is working on that right now. Python is being used for everything else so far, and as a beginning programmer, its easier to use it to jump into the code.

On the other hand, if you know C++, Python is a snap, so don't worry that what you're learning right now being useless - you'll be able to pick it up easily. If you need help feel free to join our IRC channel!

### Post by Malimbar04 on 2010-06-06
I was originally going to read through all the forums and see what designs we have set upon. Man... reading 60+ pages of forum is a bit more than I want to do right now....

Anyways, in the last few there was a question about emotions to include? I think we can streemline the original template you've been working on based on what I've learned in a few of my classes. 

The categories could obviously use some renaming:

sympathetic/parasympathetic dominance
- You have two systems that always work against each other. Sympathetic dominance is the fight/flight/freeze response.parasympathitic dominance is absolute contentment, think horny/tired/stuffed on pasta.
- I'll lable this "fff"

Nervous system EPSP/IPSP
- basically weather you're excited or depressed. excitement in real life makes you think faster(though necissarily smarter), walk faster,  play sports better, stand/sit upright with shoulders back, smile, etc.
- I'll label this "excitement"
-----
If you look at the earlier emotions, they match up to values on both of these things:

-Happy: 75% excitement, 35% fff
-cheerful: 60% excitement, 35% fff
-amused: 50% excitment, 35% fff
-peaceful: 25% excitement, 20% fff (a slightly lower fff than bored, closer to the sex/sleep/stuffed)
-bored: 25% excited, 50% fff (boredom has a mild amount of anxiety).
-angry: 85% excitement, 85% fff (and the personality makes this more of a fight response than the other two)
-embarrassed: 75% excitement, 75% fff (varies on personality. it is different from anger by application- flight and freeze)
-sad: 20% excitement, 65% fff (not exactly terrified, but very uncomfortable and not willing to do much about it)
-depressed: 5% excitement, 85 fff (extreme form of sadness)
-fearful: - excitement, 95% fff (flight or freeze response, your excitment doesn't matter)

-confused: caused by not understanding some action, but wanting to. Better dealt with by interests or intelligence attributes
-disgusted: caused by broken preconceptions - taboo, unusual tastes/smells, etc. the one emotion that's altogether seperate, but far more context sensitive. 

of course this allows for a lot more mundane states too, without having to come up with a word to match their meaning.

---

the sound you make in the bath ( no not that one! )
toilet flushing
a radio playing

thats just for starters, the best rule is to think of an activity and think what sound do you make when doing that.

So, moving around the house sounds, eating, bathroom noises, going out side, going up stairs.

any of those types of sound would be a great contribution.

Mike

### Post by lexen on 2010-08-28
I added a few more sound effects to the page that I had made before we started using pdsounds.org.  Hopefully we can use some of them as they are custom made for this game.

   I also updated the theme with an acoustic guitar like you asked.  Please let me know what you think about it and let me know if there is anything you would like me to change.

   In the sound effects page I have added files named "Day Time" and "Night Time" which are basically nature sounds, though you can hear some cars in the background.  I figured it would be nice to have something playing while you play the game.

   I was messing with the "la_vida.cfg" file and I can't seem to get the audio to play.  I would have thought changing "music=False" to "music=True" would make the music play in the background, but no luck.  Am I doing something wrong?

   I was thinking that it would be cool if the radio had two settings:  AM and FM.  With AM the game would look to a folder labeled "radio" and would then consider any folders in there to be stations.  So, if you had a file like ~/radio/Indie/Unseen Irony - Diet Starts Tomorrow.ogg it would be on the Indie station with the song "Diet Starts Tomorrow" with the artist "Unseen Irony."

   If the user selected FM, it would take them to one of the internet radio stations that we have put into the game.  It would be great because we would have a plethora of music for the players and it would be good for the internet radio station because they would get more listeners.

   Let me know what you think about that.  I was thinking about it at work and it just seemed like the right way to go.  It would also be cool if we could incorporate Pandora, but that would be tricky.


[Download Page]("http://www.unseenirony.com/lavida-music")


Later,
Lexen

### Post by lexen on 2010-08-30
I have never listened to Jamendo before and there is a lot of music on there!  Because it's CC I would assume we could feature it in the game without problem.  Because there is so much music, I don't think that we should just connect the game to Jamendo because we would get swamped with so much music that the quality would drop to the floor.

   One thing we could do is make a list of songs and artists that we like and only put that music on the "radio."  I imagine that we listen to Jamendo for a while and if we like a song, we put all the info into a text file on a server that the game would read from.  We would need to keep track of information like:
URL
Artist
Song Title
Album
Genre (station)
Language

   Because the files are not stored on our server, it wouldn't use up our bandwidth.  The users computer would download the txt file from our server which would point them to the Jamendo server.

---

### Post by lexen on 2010-08-30
Sorry for all the posts, I keep finding things out and getting crazy ideas for the game.

   On the Jamendo website they have the option to download a song in Ogg format via bittorrent.  How Open Source is that?  I know download times would be slower, but it would great if we could be utilizing bandwidth to the fullest and support an open source format.  I'm sure it would make programming more difficult, but the product would be top notch.

   Apparently "bittorrent" is open source and python based.  Here is the source code for it:
[http://download.bittorrent.com/dl/BitTorrent-5.3-GPL.tar.gz](http://download.bittorrent.com/dl/BitTorrent-5.3-GPL.tar.gz)

   I'm not a programmer, but I would imagine it wouldn't be too hard to get that put into the game because they are both use python.

I think we can use Project 48 (Traveling Through Space remake).  We could add it to the AM Radio (which we are still working on).  It's a little long, but I don't think that will be a problem because it will be in the background.

   On another note, I noticed that the icons we have looked a little out of date so I took the icon from the website and made them into icons for the game.  _**[Download]("http://www.unseenirony.com/commercial/la-vida/la-vida-icons.tar.gz")**_.  Let me know what you think.

I was trying to think of how to get the instillation process to be a little more user friendly and I was thinking it would nice if it downloaded the svn to /usr/share/games then copied a .desktop file to /usr/share/applications so it would have a spot on the menu.  The desktop file would look something like this:

```

[Desktop Entry]
Name=La Vida
Comment=Realtime life simulation
Categories=Application;Game;Simulation;
Exec=python /usr/share/games/la-vida/trunk/la_vida.py
Icon=/usr/share/app-install/icons/la-vida-icon-64x64.png
Terminal=false
Type=Application
```

We would need to have the icons moved to /usr/share/app-install/icons.  I am working on a .sh script that could do all that, I just need change the .desktop file so it looks like what I have above.  Here is the code so far:

```
sudo apt-get install subversion python-soya python-opengl python-pygame
zenity --info --text "La Vida will now download.  It can take a while to download, usually over 10 minutes.  The game will start when the instillation is complete."
sudo svn co https://la-vida.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/la-vida /usr/share/games/la-vida
sudo cp /usr/share/games/la-vida/branches/JDShu/data/gui/icons/la-vida-icon-64x64.png /usr/share/app-install/icons
sudo cp /usr/share/games/la-vida.desktop /usr/share/applications
python /usr/share/games/la-vida/trunk/la_vida.py
```

This all should then be matched with an uninstall.sh:

```
sudo rm -rf /usr/share/games/la-vida
sudo rm /usr/share/applications/la-vida.desktop
sudo rm /usr/share/app-install/icons/la-vida-icon-64x64.png
```

What do you guys think?  Is there a better way we can do this?

---

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-09-07
> **lexen said:**
> I think we can use Project 48 (Traveling Through Space remake).  We could add it to the AM Radio (which we are still working on).  It's a little long, but I don't think that will be a problem because it will be in the background.

   On another note, I noticed that the icons we have looked a little out of date so I took the icon from the website and made them into icons for the game.  _**[Download]("http://www.unseenirony.com/commercial/la-vida/la-vida-icons.tar.gz")**_.  Let me know what you think.

I was trying to think of how to get the instillation process to be a little more user friendly and I was thinking it would nice if it downloaded the svn to /usr/share/games then copied a .desktop file to /usr/share/applications so it would have a spot on the menu.  The desktop file would look something like this:

```

[Desktop Entry]
Name=La Vida
Comment=Realtime life simulation
Categories=Application;Game;Simulation;
Exec=python /usr/share/games/la-vida/trunk/la_vida.py
Icon=/usr/share/app-install/icons/la-vida-icon-64x64.png
Terminal=false
Type=Application
```We would need to have the icons moved to /usr/share/app-install/icons.  I am working on a .sh script that could do all that, I just need change the .desktop file so it looks like what I have above.  Here is the code so far:

```
sudo apt-get install subversion python-soya python-opengl python-pygame
zenity --info --text "La Vida will now download.  It can take a while to download, usually over 10 minutes.  The game will start when the instillation is complete."
sudo svn co https://la-vida.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/la-vida /usr/share/games/la-vida
sudo cp /usr/share/games/la-vida/branches/JDShu/data/gui/icons/la-vida-icon-64x64.png /usr/share/app-install/icons
sudo cp /usr/share/games/la-vida.desktop /usr/share/applications
python /usr/share/games/la-vida/trunk/la_vida.py
```This all should then be matched with an uninstall.sh:

```
sudo rm -rf /usr/share/games/la-vida
sudo rm /usr/share/applications/la-vida.desktop
sudo rm /usr/share/app-install/icons/la-vida-icon-64x64.png
```What do you guys think?  Is there a better way we can do this?

The new icons look great! Good work. :D

### Post by dv3500ea on 2010-10-22
I have made a modification (of  the mike_hibbert branch) to make moving the character more natural (as suggested by JDShu on IRC).

My first attempt had the following behaviour:
[LIST]
[*]You right click to show the pie menu
[*]You click the move button
[*]You right click where you want the character to go
[*]You click the move button
[*]The character walks to that spot
[/LIST]

My second attempt is a modification of the first and has the following behaviour:
[LIST]
[*]You right click to show the pie menu
[*]You click the move button
[*]You click where you want the character to go
[*]The character walks to that spot
[/LIST]

I prefer the second version, although the implementation is a bit messy: it uses the original version but hides the move mode menu.

I have attached the diffs of these modifications.

### Post by dv3500ea on 2010-10-24
LaVida has been packaged!!!

It has been packaged as a [deb]("http://ubuntuone.com/p/M5p/"), an [rpm]("http://ubuntuone.com/p/M5r/") and there is a [ppa]("https://launchpad.net/~lavida-team/+archive/ppa").

Some notes:
[LIST]
[*]Yes, the version number (0.6.1) was plucked out of thin air.
[*]The game is still very much experimental and you can't do much yet. It runs though :).
[*]The PPA build is still building so isn't ready yet (24/10/10 22:20)
[*]The PPA is currently only for Lucid (I can't work out how to get it to be for multiple versions)
[*]The rpm is merely an alien conversion of the deb.
[*]LaVida can be launched by typing ```
lavida
``` in a terminal (No menu shortcut yet)
[*]See ```
man lavida
``` for more details.
[/LIST]

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-12-11
Actually pretty much all the GFX is done using Soya3d so you dont really have to learn opengl as the api for soya is very much simplified 

At this point we are building the GUI as the main 3d rendering is at a point where it does enough for the time being.

So the main bulk of whats left on the road map is to get a gui that can display the dudes stats like health etc.

if we can get that going then we have a possibility to have a basic, maybe even playable system.

Mike

---

### Post by panthar91 on 2010-12-12
well i checked out soya yesterday and i do like how well documented it is.

if i was working on a gui would i have my own branch for it or would it just be merged into the main if its good enough?

---

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2010-12-12
> **panthar91 said:**
> well i checked out soya yesterday and i do like how well documented it is.

if i was working on a gui would i have my own branch for it or would it just be merged into the main if its good enough?


Well first off you can provide DIFFs that we will accept as patches.

Once your a more regular contributor we can arrange to get you your own SVN branch were you can do more complex stuff.

The best place to start is look at my branch 'mike_hibbert' to see how we are implementing GUI elements as I've already started making a basic dashboard and a right click actions menu.

The idea is that the main GUI container will feed positioning and info into each widget so you should be thinking along the lines of a parent -> child setup for each GUI control you make.

If you happy to just extend the existing GUI stuff I've done then I'm more than happy for any work you can contribute on that.

Mike

---

### Post by myromance123 on 2010-12-15
The developmental files of La Vida have always been available for download, and now there are more ways to do it.

First off, have you tried the automatic script here?
[http://www.la-vida-game.co.uk/?page_id=22]("http://www.la-vida-game.co.uk/?page_id=22")

There is also the PPA, check this previous comment by dv3500ea:
[#722]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=10021336&postcount=722")

*note: at the moment, this does not seem to work on 10.10.

There is also the manual method here:
[http://www.la-vida-game.co.uk/?page_id=24]("http://www.la-vida-game.co.uk/?page_id=24")

After either doing the manual method or the script, please follow the instructions here to get the game running:
[http://www.la-vida-game.co.uk/?page_id=26]("http://www.la-vida-game.co.uk/?page_id=26")

Don't hesitate to ask here if you are unsure about something or you can't get it running! :)

### Post by Noraphalem on 2010-12-28
> **smd0665 said:**
> It's awesome that you guys are still working on this! I wanted to take a look at it, but I'm getting an error message: 



Am I missing something?
Thank you for your work!

In the dependencies.txt file is a list with the dependencies which have to be installed:

```
Dependencies 
------------ 
 
 
INFO: The package names are taken from the Ubuntu repository. 
 
 
The python base runtime environment: 
python        2.6.6    OK 
python2.5    2.5.7    OK 
python2.6    2.6.6    OK 
python2.7    2.7    Not working    Soya is missing 
python3        3.1.3    Not working    Soya is missing 
python3.1    3.1.2    Not working    Soya is missing 
 
Python modules needed: 
numpy        Math library for arrays for python. 
pygame        SDL binding and game development library for Python. 
python-opengl    OpenGL binding for Python. 
python-soya    High level 3D engine for Python. 
 
 
Please send an email to hibbert.michael@googlemail.com if something is missing.
```

This version of the dependencies.txt is in the current svn only.

Greetings :D

### Post by dagoth_pie on 2011-06-09

One thing that I would like to put forward, is keeping the game art, under a free license. However I think that once this game reaches a playable state we'll find ourselves flooded with user created content, mostly wall and floor textures. But I think that having freely available art would be useful for programmers wanting to start a game project, although seeing as Mickey is the project lead and the one generating some revenue to get game art in the first place, I guess it's his call.

### Post by JDShu on 2011-06-09
> **dagoth_pie said:**
> 
One thing that I would like to put forward, is keeping the game art, under a free license. Most open source games while leaving the code free, use a separate license to lock the game art, keeping it in the game for the sake of uniqueness. That said, I don't think awesome game models is a priority at the moment. It's much more important that we get the game working. Noraphalem's idea of separating server and client seems to be a good idea, as we can make a text based or 2D client for game testing.

### Post by Noraphalem on 2011-06-23
For all who are curious what I am doing:

I am currently working on a way to seperate the simulation itself from the user interface/representation of what's going on. And I have achieved a very basic but running server which runs a simple simulation.

Features so far:
- A Twisted reactor which handles incoming connections (from the clients) and multithreading (the simulation runs in its own thread)
- A simulation world with its own time handling (game time instead of os time) which can be scaled (run the simulation slower or faster)
- Characters (Should I call the class Dude?) with needs and doing activities to satisfy the needs.
- Characters interact with objects in the world.

Next steps:
- Characters interact with other characters. (Not to hard. Code can taken from object interaction and modified)
- Budget and money in general.

Future:
- Personality, spyche/mood.
- Clothing as a gameplay feature. Maybe as a modifier of the opposites spyche/mood.

I am open for specific ideas. If you have a rough idea which needs some care I would suggest to discuss it here or in the IRC ([http://www.la-vida-game.co.uk/?page_id=5](http://www.la-vida-game.co.uk/?page_id=5)) before you ask for an implementation.

Greetings.

---

### Post by Noraphalem on 2011-06-27
For everyone who wants to know how to print text in the console on a defined position:

```
class asciiMapView:
    # A simple map view in ASCII art style.
    
    def __init__( self, world ):
        self.cmdPrefix = '\033['
        self.cmdSeperator = ';'
        self.cmdPostfixPosition = 'H'
        self.cmdPostfixColor = 'm'
        self.world = world
        
    def printWidget( self, posX, posY ):
        cmdPosition = '%s%i%s%i%s' % ( self.cmdPrefix, posX, self.cmdSeperator, posY, self.cmdPostfixPosition )
        print '%sThis is a test for the text position.' % cmdPosition        
        
mapView = asciiMapView( 'world' )

mapView.printWidget( 10, 10 )
```The magic does the simple escape sequence: ```
\033[<x>;<y>H
```This technique should also work in other language with proper stdout support.

EDIT:
Here is a first impression for the ASCII interface I am currently working on. Sorry but at the moment it is very minimalistic. If someone is aware of graphics programming (in Python if possible) I would be more as happy about help.

[[img]http://img4.fotos-hochladen.net/thumbnail/firstasciiintn5t19yweaq_thumb.jpg[/img]](http://www.fotos-hochladen.net/view/firstasciiintn5t19yweaq.png)

### Post by Mickeysofine1972 on 2011-11-28
One point I would like to make about the code is that its built in the way it is for some very important reasons.

I built it with a singleton to then process lots of classes through  a pipe-lining system that will be robust enough to let all objects and entities in the game environment to be informed of events and actions throughout the whole system. 

This leads to some very abstract looking classes that dont really give much clues as to how they fit together.

The end goal is that other developers, (people who are not me), would then write code using the classes as a framework.

It not my intention for anyone to start writing code for the framework, (not unless they want to), so the bulk of development should be going into developing house hold items and the actions and events they require. The end result being an activity that can be performed by your 'dude' so that he can do things like clean themselves or cook a meal etc.

I the words of Einstein "Make everything as simple as possible, but not simpler."

Hence the complexity :D

Mike

---

If I'm completely wrong then it's because I haven't paid any attention to this for a great many months.

### Post by JDShu on 2011-12-13
All right, I looked at the source again to remind myself about what needs to be done.

A couple issues:

I am currently of the opinion that the biggest issue right now is that the various layers of abstraction are bleeding all over the place, making the code unreadable. Over this winter break, I will start a new git repository that clones the current svn trunk and start doing massive cleanup. Hopefully when everything is modularized properly, we can have new contributors work on various aspects without destroying things.

Less importantly, I'd like to change the coding style to the standard PEP8 because there is no reason to use something else if we're using Python. Normally this is a bad idea, but I think the current codebase of La Vida is small enough that it can be done without too much hassle.

Even less importantly, I think Soya3D is probably not a good library to rely on given its lack of activity and that it's nowhere near production release. This is not critical, but I'll look into Panda3D as a possible replacement, as it has a much healthier community. The alternative is to contribute upstream into Soya3D so that it fulfills our needs. I won't do anything about this yet, especially since it would be done after the cleanup, but it bears thinking about.

Let me remind people that we have an IRC channel #lavida on freenode. It is quite empty but I am on most of the time to answer questions. Like most IRC channels, if I don't reply immediately, then stick around. Eventually I'll get back to my computer to answer you :)

---

### Post by JDShu on 2011-12-14
**Plan Update:**

I imported it into [github]("https://github.com/JDShu/La-Vida") (hooray for github svn imports!) My hardest exam is today (honestly I should be studying), and then I'll start spending some time.

**What needs to be done:**

[B]Get it to run

[/B]I haven't spent a lot of time yet, but I can't trivially get the current code to run. It seems to be incompatible with the latest Soya3D library which might even be incompatible with a newish distribution. This is a priority, and I hope to get it at least running in the next few days.

**Code Cleanup - namespaces:** 

RIght now the namespaces in all the modules are horribly polluted.  The modules are full of such monstrosities:

```
from some_package import *
```We need to identify what names these packages have and are used in the module in question and change it to:

```
from some_package import SomeName, SomeOtherName
```Anybody can help with this! Start a new Github account, clone my branch, make the above modifications, and send a pull request. It's easy!
[B]
Code Cleanup - PEP8

[/B]La Vida is written in Python, and Python has a default style known as [PEP8. ]("http://www.python.org/dev/peps/pep-0008/")Right now it's in a C-like style that is really not needed in Python. It makes use of some redundant conventions that are great in C but not in Python. In addition, there is no reason to be different just because we can. People can easily contribute to this as well. Read the PEP8 style guide and make changes so that the La Vida code follows it. Send a pull request and done!

[B]Soya3D -> Panda3D

[/B]Switching to a higher level library instead of rolling our own OGL code was the right idea, but I've had so much trouble getting the Soya library and getting it to work with the current code that I think I *will* try to replace Soya with Panda over the winter break. Documentation for Soya is ridiculously lacking and the last release candidate update was a year ago. Since we need to encapsulate these external library calls into separate modules anyway, I think it won't be too much wasted effort. This is not a trivial task, but people with good Python experience are encouraged to help, (or do it for me? :P)

There's other stuff that needs to be done as well such as writing tests and moving modules around so that they make more sense. My hope is that by the end of January, we'll have code of high enough quality that other people can jump in and add improvements without understanding the entire code base. After that class starts again for me (and my new job) so I'm not certain how much free time I'll have especially since there's other stuff I want to play with as well.

---

### Post by Sofox on 2012-08-02
Hey Mike,

IndieGoGo seems to be the most popularalternative to Kickstarter where you don't have to be a US resident to start a campaign.

A bunch of us here have been following the crowdfunding scene and would be happy to give advice or help  (check [here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=12128332&postcount=3") and [here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=2023992"))

Also, while I was about to give you the standard spiel about proving you can make the game and having promotional materials etc, it occurs to me that this one of the first real open source games to go crowdfunding (OverDose kinda was, but they never pushed the OS angle, Novacut was an OS film editor that succeeded on their second try after raising awareness). My point is, if you start the campaign and make a reasonable demonstration that you'll really develop this, then you'll have a lot of help in the OS community spreading word and pledging money. (this is especially so as new methods to get high quality OS games are always apprecaited)

### Post by Sofox on 2012-08-02
Hey Mike, 
Okay, I've pledged, but there are some problems with your page.

Leading a crowdfunding campaign isn't just making a page and leaving it like that (I should have told you this earlier), but requires a lot of effort on your behalf and you'll need to make a lot of changes to it throughout the campaign.

Firstly, rewards tiers need work. What happens if someone donates $25? If the answer is "nothing", it's gonna be a hard sell. (You can't change reward tiers after someone donates to them, but you should be able to add tiers no problem).

Second, the intro video needs an introduction. A tech demo doesn't cut it. You need to succinctly explain what the game is about and how far you intend it to go.

Thirdly: Any way you can get some placeholder art? Preferably of a decent quality? For both video and screenshots they're vital for information. Humans are visually orientated creatures.

Fourthly: Your open source status is a unique selling point. Along with promoting it, you should specify the exact license that you want to release the game under and whether the art assets are under the same license.

Other than that, crowdsourcing has been around long enough for people to learn various ways of helping this along. This post: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=12128332](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=12128332) contains several linked articles and advice (mostly from madjr) about Crowdfunding campaigns. Hopefully Madjr himself will give some thoughts on this campaign.

Other than that, wishing you the best. Let's really push this forward.

---
